5.3 Academic integrity 
 
Murdoch University expects students and staff to pursue the highest standards of integrity in all academic activity. 
Academic integrity involves behaving ethically and honestly in scholarship and relies on respect for others’ ideas through 
proper acknowledgement and referencing of publications.  
Academic misconduct is treated seriously and penalties may apply.  
More information about academic integrity can be found at https://goto.murdoch.edu.au/learningstudy. To help you learn 
about academic integrity practices, all students are required to complete the Murdoch Academic Passport (MAP100) . 
Please also note the library citation guide. 
Murdoch University makes use of content matching software to detect submitted work that is not original. When you 
submit an assessment to myMurdoch Learning, it is checked by this software. Your Unit Coordinator may apply other 
processes to verify that your submitted assessment is your own work. 
In this unit, we undertake these practices to assure academic integrity:  
• Your Unit Co-ordinators may use software found in LMS as well as other code and document matching software 
when viewing work that you submit. This pattern -matching systems/software are designed to compare work 
submitted by students with other sources from the internet, journals/periodicals, other students, and previous 
submissions. Its primary purpose is to detect any submitted work that is not original and provide a thorough 
comparison between the submitted document and the original sources. 
• You may be asked to attend interview or to provide explanation of your submission. Make sure you understand 
everything you are submitting. 
• Read the assignment and examination sheets for any other process. 
 
5.4 Acceptable use of Generative AI 
(adapted from a relevant policy written by Dr. David Murray)  
Generative AI, a subset of artificial intelligence, is a rapidly evolving technology that has the potential to revolutionize 
our work, and the world, as we know it. This technology will likely be transformative, and as educators we have the job 
of walking a tightrope of adequately preparing you with fundamental skills and allowing you to move into your work life 
with exposure and skill with the state-of-the-art tools. You should expect a mix of tasks, with some tasks preventing its 
use and some tasks permitting its use. You should use this policy as a default guide in this unit. Unless there is more 
specific information related to the task fall back on these guidelines on the appropriate use of this technology.  
Generative AI refers to algorithms and models that can generate new content. They can create anything from written 
text, to images, music, and even code. Some of the most popular generative models include GPT -3, DALL-E, and 
CoPilot. My recommendation is th at you use Microsoft’s CoPilot https://copilot.microsoft.com/ where you have free 
access and your data is protected. My advice is that you spend some time working with AI such that you are proficient 
in its use. I do, however, want to mark your work, and so the following are guidelines for the appropriate use.  
You should use generative AI for learning like you would a friend or colleague. Here are some things you would never 
do with a friend or colleague:  
1. Ask them to write your report or documentation for you and attach your name to it  
2. Give them the problem and ask them to write the code for you  
3. Give them a write up of a task, and ask them to improve the level of language to a university level  
4. Get them to write Powerpoint slides for you.  

ICT167_UIG_2024_S2_v1.1.pdf : CONTENT:  Principles of Computer Science Page 10 of 15 
Assignments are to be submitted via LMS via your MyUnits page by the due date. Details of assignment submission are 
given on the assignment question sheet. Please note that the submission can take up to 10 minutes. Do not forget to 
press the [Submit] button after loading the assignment on to the LMS. 
If you cannot complete all the questions in an assignment, you may wish to submit what you have completed by the due 
date. If you need an extension for an assignment, contact the unit coordinator by email before the due date. Extensions 
are granted only in exceptional circumstances . In requesting an extension, you should provide appropriate 
documentation such as a medical certificate and suggest for consideration a schedule for submission which meets your 
circumstances. Alternative work may be required if information about the solution has been distributed or assignments 
returned. If you are granted an extension, you should save a copy of the e -mail from the Unit Coordinator confirming 
this and include this with your assignment when you submit it. 
Unless you have obtained a prior extension to the submission deadline, be advised that late submissions will incur a 
penalty of 10% deduction per day late, based upon the total possible mark for the assignment. 
Assignments must be presented in a professional manner. Please adhere to the following guidelines: 
I. The external documentation must be saved in Microsoft Word format. It should include your details (name, 
student number, your tutor’s name) and a Table of Contents which reflects the actual current contents of the 
submission. The details of the external documentation required will be given on the Assignment question sheet. 
It is your responsibility to read the assignment specification carefully. Sample test data and results from a 
program run can be copied on to a Word file (copy from the program output win dow and paste to a Word file) 
and submitted as part of the external documentation. 
II. Number all pages, including diagrams, in the Word document. 
III. Compress your documentation and Java program files in a .zip file before submitting. Make sure that all 
necessary files are submitted so that the programs can be viewed, compiled and run successfully. Note that the 
whole NetBeans project folder can be zipped. 
IV. Your User Guide for each question should include clear instructions on how to access, compile and run each 
program. 
For each assignment question, the material that should be submitted and is specific to the question will be described as 
part of that question. Even if you do not succeed in obtaining a complete working program, you should still submit what 
you have been able to accomplish, including how you might have tested the program in order to check its correctness. 
With regard to the actual program, you should pay particular attention to the following points as these will be taken into 
account when marking your submissions: 
• General layout of the program, 
• Your name and purpose comment at the beginning of program, 
• Useful comments throughout the program, 
• Meaningful identifier names 
• Modular structure of program 
• Your comments on your program’s performance/limitations

5.2 Assessment information 
5.2.1 Assessment 1 – Laboratory work 
ASSESSMENT DESCRIPTION 
The laboratory work will be assessed on an on-going basis. Internal students are required to demonstrate their laboratory 
work during the lab sessions (online or face-to-face) on a weekly basis. External students will be required to submit it to 
their tutor at regular intervals for checking and feedback. External students may be requested to explain the submission 
to the tutor on requests. 
Details of the assessment and the submission will be available in the tutorial sheets 
 
5.2.2 Assessment 2 – Assignments 
ASSESSMENT DESCRIPTION 
Details for submission of assignments including the actual due dates will be given on the assignment question sheets. 
Please read the assignment question sheet carefully and pay close attention to all of the instructions as assignments 
which do not meet th ese criteria may lose marks. Assignments will be made available several weeks before they are 
due. Check the unit's LMS site and announcements on the unit’s LMS Announcements page. 
 
HOW TO SUBMIT  
Make sure you understand what you submit in your assignment as you may be called to explain your 
submission in person (or online platform) by your tutor.

ICT167_UIG_2024_S2_v1.1.pdf : CONTENT:  Principles of Computer Science Page 7 of 15 
Try Writing a Summary or Code 
If you want to test whether or not you have mastered a section, try writing out a summary of its contents (or 
code) without looking at the unit material. If you succeed (and the summary or code is correct) then you certainly 
know the work. If you do not qu ite manage all of it, at least you will know what to revise. And always illustrate 
the concepts by writing some Java code. You need to know the code, do not rely on IDE prompts. 
Write Programs and Try Problems as You Meet Them 
Nearly all of the topics have programming exercises prescribed. As you work through these you will gain 
experience with the operating system and compiler and develop your skills in programming and debugging. If 
you get stuck on a problem, it may pay to lay it aside and come back to it another day. If you receive comments 
from your tutor, use them to review your work. If in doubt, ask the tutor for further explanations. 
Contact Your Tutor 
You should not spend an unreasonably long time on one problem. Go on to something else and get in touch 
with your tutor for some help. Prepare a list of questions you wish to ask. When you telephone (or email) your 
tutor, you should have your unit notes an d the list of questions with you, so that you do not waste time (and 
money) searching for information during your conversation with the tutor. 
 
3.2.2 Learning activities and details 
Contact time 
Online Lectures: 2 hours/week 
Laboratory session: 2 hours/week  
Attendance requirements 
Internal students are expected to attend two hours of online lectures and one 2 -hour practice session each week. All 
internal students are required to enrol to one of the 2 -hour session. Regardless of whether you are doing face -to-
face or online practice sessions, you will need to explain your code submissions to your tutor/lecturer. Online 
and external students will do the explanation on online platform. 
No on-campus attendance is required for external students. You may be called by your tutor to explain the code of your 
submissions. However, you are welcome to attend as many of the on -campus lectures as you wish. Please visit the 
following web site for links to the teaching timetable http://our.murdoch.edu.au/Students/ 
Small group and interactive teaching and learning activities 
Internal students have two hours of lab sessions (in addition to two hours of lectures), both hours being supervised by 
a tutor. Attendance at these lab sessions is absolutely essential. Students who miss even a small number of sessions 
can quickly fall behind and are often unable to catch up and may end up having to withdraw from the unit or failing the 
unit. Each lab session begins with a discussion, initiated by the tutor, about the current week’s work and the 
programming concepts relevant to the week. I n the second hour, the tutor checks the student’s work if complete and 
answers any questions they may have. 
3.3 Suggested time commitment 
As this is a 3 credit point unit, we expect you to spend on average 10 hours per week for the total weeks of this 
teaching period (or about 150 hours overall) working on this unit. 

ICT167_UIG_2024_S2_v1.1.pdf : CONTENT:  Principles of Computer Science Page 6 of 15 
3 How to study this unit 
 
3.1 Approach to learning 
3.1.1 Learning approach underpinning unit 
The unit material is divided into 11 topics and associated practice work. For internal students, there is a two-hour online 
lecture and a two -hour practice session each week. The practice sessions are used to exercise and reinforce 
knowledge of the unit material and are a vital part of the learning activities of the unit. External students need to 
work through the exercises as well. You will also need to spend time on reading and do the practical work outside the 
scheduled hours in order to fully understand the unit material. It will help your understanding of the material if you read 
the relevant text book chapter in conjunction with the notes for each lecture topic. 
Reading and memorising the concepts without understanding and code them using Java  is not enough. Make 
sure you know how to apply the concepts learned by coding them in Java to solve a problem given. It is therefore 
very important for you to complete all the Practice Work (lab exercises) and assignments on your own. Try to write your 
code on paper  or MS Word  without using IDE, this is the common practice used by software developing companies 
used in their interview sessions. 
Although this unit uses Java as a programming language to learn the object-oriented concepts, you should be able to 
apply the learned concepts to other programming languages (e.g. Python). 
Some of you will have already developed effective studying habits. What works well for one person may not for another, 
and so it is important that you find a method that suits you.  However, the system described below seems to work well 
for most people. 
 
3.1.2 Unit changes in response to student feedback 
Numerous changes have been made to the unit in response to student and industry feedback. Lecture notes have been 
expanded to include more examples and updated to incorporate concepts in object-oriented programming and design 
patterns. The lab sessions have also been revised accordingly. 
3.2 Learning activities & requirements 
3.2.1 Overall expectations 
Read the Study Guide 
Quickly read through the introduction and Topics in the Unit Information Guide so that you are aware of the 
topics to be studied and the unit objectives. Note the Readings for each topic in the Unit Information Guide. 
Note any information on Practice Work and assignments. These will be made available progressively at the 
unit’s LMS site. 
Check on the textbook and the computing equipment and software required. Arrange to get these essential 
requirements as quickly as possible. 
Work in Sections 
Tackle the work in sections, trying to master each one before going on to the next. In each section read the unit 
material and relevant sections of the textbook. Do the regular practical work. Be consistent, do it over the whole 
semester. Most students will face difficulties if they leave all the work to the end of the semester.

ICT167_UIG_2024_S2_v1.1.pdf : CONTENT:  Principles of Computer Science Page 3 of 15 
1 Unit information 
Welcome to: 
ICT167 
Principles of Computer Science 
1.1 Unit Overview 
This unit is designed to develop the skills of problem solving and program design using an Object Oriented programming 
language. It assumes that you have passed an introductory unit in programming, such as ICT159 Foundations of 
Programming. ICT167 will use  the Java language for practical work to develop your programming skills. Major topics 
include: algorithm design; procedural abstractions; the concepts of pre- and post-conditions; strings, arrays, introduction 
to object -oriented concepts including data ab straction, encapsulation, classes and object references, inheritance; 
introduction to recursion; streams and file input and output; the definition and use of common classes like lists, stacks 
and queues. 
 
Prerequisites 
ICT159 Foundations of Programming. 
Note: Students must either have passed ICT159 Foundations of Programming or been formally granted an exemption 
from it. Exemptions must be approved by the Unit Coordinator and the Academic Chair. 
NOTE: It is very important that you understand all the concepts and programming techniques covered in ICT159 
before doing this unit. 
 
1.2 Learning outcomes 
This unit enables you to demonstrate your achievement of the following unit learning outcomes. 
Unit Learning Outcomes 
1.  Demonstrate the use of the object-oriented approach to design, implement, test and document solutions to problems. 
2. Demonstrate understanding of the mechanics of parameter passing in the context of object -oriented programming, 
and how to use the class mechanism to support encapsulation and information hiding. 
3. Design, implement and test the implementation of hierarchical relationships among objects using class hierarchy and 
inheritance. 
4. Write and use arrays, strings, files, lists, stacks and queues in object-oriented programs. 
5.  Explain algorithm complexity and demonstrate the ability to select appropriate algorithms and structures for specified 
problems.

ICT167-Exam_2024.pdf : CONTENT: Example questions
• Give Java code for a client program which uses the Mammal 
class to do the following. It will create a Mammal object using 
the default constructor. It will then get the name and age of a 
mammal from the user and set the Mammal object to the 
input values. The program will then get the name and age of a 
second mammal from the user and create the second 
mammal object using the non-default constructor. It will then 
determine whether or not the two mammals are the same 
and display this information. Finally, the program will print out 
the details of the two mammals.

ICT167-Exam_2024.pdf : CONTENT: Example questions
(15 marks)
Suppose that a Mammal class written in Java is already available which you 
can use (i.e., you are not asked to write this class). This class has instance 
variables, constructors and methods as described below:
1. instance variables that represent a mammal’s name as a String and the 
mammal’s age as an integer
2. a default constructor
3. a constructor which is given a mammal’s name as a String and the 
mammal’s age as an integer
4. a method set (…) for setting the name and age of a mammal
5. a method named printDetails() that prints out the name and the age of 
the mammal
6. an equals(…) method which compares the parameter of mammal class to 
the current object and returns true if two mammals have the same name 
and same age

ICT_167_PAST_PAPER_EXAM.pdf.pdf : CONTENT: Answer 2
a).
- Definition:
Top-downtestingisanincremental approachtotesting, wherethehighest level modulesaretestedfirstandthenprogressivelylower-level modulesareintegratedandtested. Inthisapproach, themaincontrolmoduleistestedearly, andstubsareusedtosimulatethelower-level modulesthat arenot yet integrated.Aslower-level modulesbecomeavailable, theyreplacethestubsandareintegratedintotheoverallsystem.
Bottom-uptestingstartswiththetestingof thelowest level unitsor modulesfirst. Thesemodulesaretestedindependentlyusingdriversthat simulatehigher-level modules. Oncetheselower-level modulesaretestedandvalidated, theyareintegratedtotest higher-level modules, progressingupwardsuntil theentiresystemisintegratedandtested.
- Differences:
Top-downtestingstartsfromthetop(mainmodule) andmovesdownward, whereasbottom-uptestingstartsfromthebottom(leaf modules) andmovesupward.
Top-downtestingusesstubstosimulatelower-level modules, whilebottom-uptestingusesdriverstosimulatehigher-level modules.
Top-downtestingfocusesontheintegrationof high-level functionalitiesfirst, whereasbottom-uptestingensuresthat lower-level functionalitiesaretestedandvalidatedbeforemovingtohigher levels.
Intop-downtesting, themaincontrol logicor user interfaceistestedearly. Inbottom-uptesting, userinterfacetestingisdonelater intheintegrationprocess.
b).
(i) Output tothescreenthestringwhichislarger inlength:
if (s1.length() >s2.length()) {System.out.println(s1);} elseif (s1.length() <s2.length()) {System.out.println(s2);} else{System.out.println("Bothstringsareof equal length.");}

Answer 1
a).
(i) TheJVMisanabstract computingmachinethat enablesacomputer torunaJavaprogram. It convertsJavabytecodeintomachinelanguagesothat it canbeexecutedbythecomputer’shardware.
(ii) Acompiler isasoftwaretool that translatessourcecodewritteninahigh-level programminglanguageintomachinecode, bytecode, or another programminglanguage. For Java, thecompiler translatesJavasourcecodeintobytecode.
(iii) AclassinJavaisablueprint for creatingobjects. It definesthedatafields(attributes) andmethods(functions) that objectscreatedfromtheclasscanhave.
(iv) Aconstructor isaspecial methodinaclassthat iscalledwhenanobject of that classisinstantiated. Itusuallyinitializesthenewobject andsetsinitial valuesfor itsattributes.
(v) Aninstancevariableisavariabledefinedinaclassfor whicheachinstantiatedobject of theclasshasitsownseparatecopy. Thesevariablesrepresent thestateor propertiesof theobject.
(vi) Pass-by-referencemeanspassingareferencetotheactual memoryaddressof thevariableratherthanacopyof thevariable’svalue. Javausespass-by-value, but for objects, thevalueisthereferencetotheobject, whichcanmakeit seemlikepass-by-reference.
(vii): Dataabstractionisaprincipleinobject-orientedprogrammingthat allowsaprogrammer tohideallbut therelevant dataabout anobject inorder toreducecomplexityandincreaseefficiency. It involvescreatingsimpleinterfacesandhidingcompleximplementationdetails.
(viii) MethodoverloadinginJavaistheabilitytocreatemultiplemethodsinthesameclasswiththesamenamebut different parameters(different type, number, or both). It allowsmethodstoperformsimilar butslightlydifferent functions.
(ix) Assertionsareadebuggingaidthat teststhetruthof aconditionintheprogram. Whenanassertionisexecuted, it evaluatesaBooleanexpressionandif theexpressionisfalse, it throwsanAssertionError,indicatingalogical error inthecode.
(x) Inheritanceisanobject-orientedprogrammingconcept whereanewclassiscreatedfromanexistingclass. Thenewclass(subclass) inheritsfieldsandmethodsfromtheexistingclass(superclass), enablingcodereuseandthecreationof hierarchical relationshipsbetweenclasses.

ICT167-Exam_2024.pdf : CONTENT: Example questions
• Give Java code for a client program which uses the Mammal 
class to do the following. It will create a Mammal object using 
the default constructor. It will then get the name and age of a 
mammal from the user and set the Mammal object to the 
input values. The program will then get the name and age of a 
second mammal from the user and create the second 
mammal object using the non-default constructor. It will then 
determine whether or not the two mammals are the same 
and display this information. Finally, the program will print out 
the details of the two mammals.

ICT167-Exam_2024.pdf : CONTENT: Example questions
(15 marks)
Suppose that a Mammal class written in Java is already available which you 
can use (i.e., you are not asked to write this class). This class has instance 
variables, constructors and methods as described below:
1. instance variables that represent a mammal’s name as a String and the 
mammal’s age as an integer
2. a default constructor
3. a constructor which is given a mammal’s name as a String and the 
mammal’s age as an integer
4. a method set (…) for setting the name and age of a mammal
5. a method named printDetails() that prints out the name and the age of 
the mammal
6. an equals(…) method which compares the parameter of mammal class to 
the current object and returns true if two mammals have the same name 
and same age
